\section{Supplementary Material for `The complex network of trophic
interactions in a subAntarctic oceanic Marine Protected
Area'}\label{supplementary-material-for-the-complex-network-of-trophic-interactions-in-a-subantarctic-oceanic-marine-protected-area}

\subsection{Methodology}\label{methodology}

\subsubsection{Food web construction}\label{food-web-construction}

The following figure and tables summarise the data we used to build the
network of trophic (predator-prey) interactions for the Marine Protected
Area Namuncur√° - Banco Burdwood I ecosystem. Figure \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{1 }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{2 }\DIFaddend resumes the type
and number of references reviewed. Table 1 is the complete list of
trophic interactions and references that confirm each of them. Table 2
is the species list with details on trophic species cases (aggregated
taxa).

\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{With the gathered trophic data, we constructed a matrix of pairwise
interactions; a value of 1 or 0 was assigned to each element a\_ij of
the matrix depending on whether the predator j preyed or not on the prey
i. Then we transformed such a matrix into an oriented graph with L
trophic interactions between S nodes or species (Figure 1).
}

\DIFaddend \begin{figure}
\DIFaddbeginFL 

{\DIFaddendFL \centering \DIFdelbeginFL %DIFDELCMD < \includegraphics{SupMaterial_files/figure-latex/ref_plot-1.pdf}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \includegraphics[width=12cm]{FigS1} 

}

\DIFaddendFL \caption{\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Summary }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Matrix }\DIFaddendFL of \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{references used to build }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{pairwise interactions and }\DIFaddendFL the \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{network of trophic
}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{oriented graph }\DIFaddendFL (\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{predator-prey}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{food web}\DIFaddendFL ) \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{interactions for the MPAN-BB ecosystem}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{derived from it}\DIFaddendFL . \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Number of species S = 9, number of interactions (L) = 15.}\DIFaddendFL }\DIFaddbeginFL \label{fig:unnamed-chunk-1}
\DIFaddendFL \end{figure}

\DIFaddbegin \subsubsection{\DIFadd{Network analysis}}\label{network-analysis}

\DIFadd{Trophic level
}

\DIFadd{Trophic levels (TL) of species were calculated using the shortweighted
TL formula of Williams and Martinez (2004). Shortweighted trophic level
is defined as the average of the shortest TL and prey-averaged TL.
Shortest TL of a consumer in a food web is equal to 1 + the shortest
chain length from this consumer to any basal species (Williams and
Martinez, 2004). Prey averaged TL is equal to 1 + the mean TL of all
consumer's trophic resources, calculated as:
}

\begin{equation}
\DIFadd{TL_j = 1 + \sum_{i = 1}^{S} l_{ij} \frac{TL_i}{n_j}
}\end{equation}

\DIFadd{where \(TL_j\) is the trophic level of species \(j\); \(S\) is the
number of species in the food web; \(l_{ij}\) is the connection matrix
with \(S\) rows and \(S\) columns, in which for column \(j\) and row
\(i\), \(l_{ij}\) = 1 if species \(j\) consumes species \(i\) and
\(l_{ij}\) = 0 if not; and \(n_j\) is the number of prey species in the
diet of species \(j\). For basal species TL = 1 given that they have no
prey.
}

\DIFadd{Topological roles
}

\DIFadd{Beforehand, we need to calculate modularity. Modularity was calculated
as the difference between realized and expected within-modules
interactions, divided by the total number of interactions. We used a
stochastic algorithm called ``simulated annealing'' (Guimer√† and Nunes
Amaral, 2005), that assumes that the nodes of the same module have more
links than one would expect in a random network. The modules are
obtained from dividing all the nodes in the network to maximize
modularity. In this way, the modularity index is defined as:
}

\begin{equation}
\DIFadd{M = \sum_{s} (\frac{I_s}{L} - (\frac{d_s}{2L})^2)
}\end{equation}

\DIFadd{where \(s\) is the number of modules or compartments, \(I_s\) is the
number of links between species in the modules, \(d_s\) is the sum of
degrees for all species in module \(s\) and \(L\) is the total number of
links.
}

\DIFadd{Species topological roles were calculated using the method of functional
cartography (Guimer√† and Nunes Amaral, 2005). Roles are determined
according to two parameters:
}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  \DIFadd{the standardized within-module degree (dz), a z-score that reflects
  how well a species is connected to other species inside the module,
  relative to other species within its own module:
}\end{enumerate}

\begin{equation}
\DIFadd{dz_i = \frac{k_{is}-k_s}{ks}
}\end{equation}

\DIFadd{where \(k_{is}\) is the number of links of species \(i\) within its own
module \(s\), and \(ks\) are the average and standard deviation of
\(k_{is}\) over all species in \(s\), respectively.
}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\setcounter{enumi}{1}
\tightlist
\item
  \DIFadd{the participation coefficient \(PC\), estimates the links distribution
  of species \(i\) among modules:
}\end{enumerate}

\begin{equation}
\DIFadd{PC_i = 1 - \sum_{S} \frac{k_{is}}{k_i}
}\end{equation}

\DIFadd{where \(k_i\) is the total number of links of species \(i\) and
\(k_{is}\) is the number of links of species \(i\) to species in module
\(s\). To determine the role of each species, the \(dz\) ‚àí \(PC\)
parameters space was divided into four regions (Kortsch et al., 2015),
with two threshold values: \(dz\) = 2.5 and \(PC\) = 0.625. Thus, the
species were classified as follows:
}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \DIFadd{Module hub (\(dz\) ‚â• 2.5, \(PC\) \textless{} 0.625): The species has a
  relatively high number of links, but at least 60\% within its own
  module.
}\item
  \DIFadd{Module specialist (\(dz\) \textless{} 2.5, \(PC\) \textless{} 0.625):
  The species has relatively few links and most within its own module.
}\item
  \DIFadd{Module connector (\(dz\) \textless{} 2.5, \(PC\) ‚â• 0.625): The species
  has relatively few links and most between modules.
}\item
  \DIFadd{Network connector (\(dz\) ‚â• 2.5, \(PC\) ‚â• 0.625): The species has a
  high connectivity between and within the modules.
}\end{itemize}

\DIFaddend \newpage
\begin{landscape}

\newpage

\subsection{Results}\label{results}

Table 3 presents an exhaustive list of the species-level properties for
the food web of the MPA Namuncur√° - Banco Burdwood I ecosystem.

\newpage

Figure 2 shows the species' topological roles in the food web graph.
Species, represented by circles, are coloured by role: network connector
(dark purple), module connector (light pink), module hub (light green),
and module specialist (dark green). Network connector = 1 species;
module connector = 41 species; module hub = 10 species; and module
specialist = 328 species.

\begin{figure}
\centering
\DIFdelbeginFL %DIFDELCMD < \includegraphics{SupMaterial_files/figure-latex/toprole_graph-1.pdf}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \includegraphics{RevisedSupMaterial_files/figure-latex/toprole_graph-1.pdf}
\DIFaddendFL \caption{Graph of the food web showing species coloured by topological
role: network connector (dark purple), module connector (light pink),
module hub (light green), and module specialist (dark green). Circle
diameter is relative to the number of interactions.}
\end{figure}
